<td>\n         0595031\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr class="mergedrow">\n        <th scope="row">\n         <a href="/wiki/Maryland_highway_system" title="Maryland highway system">\n          Highways\n         </a>\n        </th>\n        <td>\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Interstate_97_in_Maryland" title="Interstate 97 in Maryland">\n          I-97\n         </a>\n         ,\n         <a href="/wiki/U.S._Route_50_in_Maryland" title="U.S. Route 50 in Maryland">\n          US 50\n         </a>\n         ,\n         <a href="/wiki/U.S._Route_301_in_Maryland" title="U.S. class="external text" href="http://www.annapolis.gov/" rel="nofollow">\n          www.annapolis.gov\n         </a>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <p>\n       <b>\n        Annapolis\n       </b>\n       (\n       <span class="nowrap">\n        <span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt">\n         <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">\n          /\n          <span style="border-bottom:1px dotted">\n           <span title="/\xc9\x99/: \'a\' in \'about\'">\n            \xc9\x99\n           </span>\n           <span title="/\xcb\x88/: primary stress follows">\n            \xcb\x88\n           </span>\n           <span title="\'n\' in \'nigh\'">\n            n\n           </span>\n           <span title="/\xc3\xa6/: \'a\' in \'bad\'">\n            \xc3\xa6\n           </span>\n           <span title="\'p\' in \'pie\'">\n            p\n           </span>\n           <span title="/\xc9\x99l/: \'le\' in \'bottle\'">\n            \xc9\x99l\n           </span>\n           <span title="/\xc9\xaa/: \'i\' in \'kit\'">\n            \xc9\xaa\n           </span>\n           <span title="\'s\' in \'sigh\'">\n            s\n           </span>\n          </span>\n          /\n         </a>\n        </span>\n       </span>\n       ) is the capital of the U.S. state of\n       <a href="/wiki/Maryland" title="Maryland">\n        Maryland\n       </a>\n       , as well as the\n       <a href="/wiki/County_seat" title="County seat">\n        county seat\n       </a>\n       of\n       <a href="/wiki/Anne_Arundel_County,_Maryland" title="Anne Arundel County, Maryland">\n        Anne Arundel County\n       </a>\n       . Situated on the\n       <a href="/wiki/Chesapeake_Bay" title="Chesapeake Bay">\n        Chesapeake Bay\n       </a>\n       at the mouth of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Severn_River_(Maryland)" title="Severn River (Maryland)">\n        Severn River\n       </a>\n       , 25 miles (40\xc2\xa0km) south of\n       <a href="/wiki/Baltimore" title="Baltimore">\n        Baltimore\n       </a>\n       and about 30 miles (50\xc2\xa0km) east of\n       <a href="/wiki/Washington,_D.C." title="Washington, D.C.">\n        Washington, D.C.\n       </a>\n       , Annapolis is part of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Baltimore%E2%80%93Washington_metropolitan_area" title="Baltimore\xe2\x80\x93Washington metropolitan area">\n        Baltimore\xe2\x80\x93Washington metropolitan area\n       </a>\n       . Its population was measured at 38,394 by the\n       <a href="/wiki/2010_United_States_Census" title="2010 United States Census">\n        2010 census\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The city served as the seat of the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Confederation_Congress" title="Confederation Congress">\n        Confederation Congress\n       </a>\n       (former Second\n       <a href="/wiki/Continental_Congress" title="Continental Congress">\n        Continental Congress\n       </a>\n       ) and temporary national capital of the\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">\n        United States\n       </a>\n       in 1783\xe2\x80\x931784. At that time, General\n       <a href="/wiki/George_Washington" title="George Washington">\n        George Washington\n       </a>\n       came before the body convened in the new\n       <a href="/wiki/Maryland_State_House" title="Maryland State House">\n        Maryland State House\n       </a>\n       and resigned his commission as commander of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Continental_Army" title="Continental Army">\n        Continental Army\n       </a>\n       . A month later, the Congress ratified the\n       <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Paris_(1783)" title="Treaty of Paris (1783)">\n        Treaty of Paris\n       </a>\n       of 1783, ending the\n       <a href="/wiki/American_Revolutionary_War" title="American Revolutionary War">\n        American Revolutionary War\n       </a>\n       , with\n       <a href="/wiki/Great_Britain" title="Great Britain">\n        Great Britain\n       </a>\n       recognizing the independence of the\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">\n        United States\n       </a>\n       . The city and state capitol was also the site of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Annapolis_Convention_(1786)" title="Annapolis Convention (1786)">\n        1786 Annapolis Convention\n       </a>\n       , which issued a call to the states to send delegates for the\n       <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_Convention_(United_States)" title="Constitutional Convention (United States)">\n        Constitutional Convention\n       </a>\n       to be held the following year in\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Philadelphia,_Pennsylvania" title="Philadelphia, Pennsylvania">\n        Philadelphia\n       </a>\n       . Over 220 years later, the\n       <a href="/wiki/Annapolis_Conference" title="Annapolis Conference">\n        Annapolis Peace Conference\n       </a>\n       , was held in 2007. Annapolis is the home of\n       <a href="/wiki/St._John%27s_College_(Annapolis/Santa_Fe)" title="St. John\'s College (Annapolis/Santa Fe)">\n        St. John\'s College\n       </a>\n       , founded 1696, as well as the\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Naval_Academy" title="United States Naval Academy">\n        United States Naval Academy\n       </a>\n       , established 1845.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n      </p>\n      <div class="toc" id="toc">\n       <div class="toctitle">\n        <h2>\n         Contents\n        </h2>\n       </div>\n       <ul>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-12">\n           <a href="#Other">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             2.6\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Other\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-13">\n           <a href="#2007_Annapolis_Conference">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             2.7\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             2007 Annapolis Conference\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n         </ul>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-14">\n         <a href="#Geography_and_climate">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           3\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Geography and climate\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-15">\n         <a href="#Demographics">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           4\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Demographics\n          </span>\n         </a>\n         <ul>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-16">\n           <a href="#2010_census">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             4.1\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             2010 census\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-17">\n           <a href="#2000_census">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             4.2\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             2000 census\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n         </ul>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-18">\n         <a href="#Economy">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           5\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Economy\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-19">\n         <a href="#Transportation">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           6\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Transportation\n          </span>\n         </a>\n         <ul>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-20">\n           <a href="#Bus">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             6.1\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Bus\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n         </ul>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-21">\n         <a href="#Government">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           7\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Government\n          </span>\n         </a>\n         <ul>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-22">\n           <a href="#City_government">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             7.1\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             City government\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-23">\n           <a href="#State_government">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             7.2\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             State government\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n         </ul>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-24">\n         <a href="#Education">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           8\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Education\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-25">\n         <a href="#Sports">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           9\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Sports\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-26">\n         <a href="#Parks_and_recreation">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           10\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Parks and recreation\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-27">\n         <a href="#Publications">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           11\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Publications\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-28">\n         <a href="#Notable_people">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           12\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Notable people\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-29">\n         <a href="#Neighborhoods_and_suburbs">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           13\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Neighborhoods and suburbs\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-30">\n         <a href="#Sister_cities">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           14\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Sister cities\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-31">\n         <a href="#See_also">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           15\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           See also\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-32">\n         <a href="#References">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           16\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           References\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-33">\n         <a href="#Further_reading">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           17\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Further reading\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-34">\n         <a href="#External_links">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           18\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           External links\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n       </ul>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="History">\n        History\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Annapolis,_Maryland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <h3>\n       <span id="Colonial_and_early_United_States_(1649\xe2\x80\x931808)">\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Colonial_and_early_United_States_.281649.E2.80.931808.29">\n        Colonial and early United States (1649\xe2\x80\x931808)\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Annapolis,_Maryland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Colonial and early United States (1649\xe2\x80\x931808)">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Annapolis_Old_Treasury_Building_from_1735_by_D_Ramey_Logan.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3000" data-file-width="4496" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Annapolis_Old_Treasury_Building_from_1735_by_D_Ramey_Logan.jpg/220px-Annapolis_Old_Treasury_Building_from_1735_by_D_Ramey_Logan.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Annapolis_Old_Treasury_Building_from_1735_by_D_Ramey_Logan.jpg/330px-Annapolis_Old_Treasury_Building_from_1735_by_D_Ramey_Logan.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Annapolis_Old_Treasury_Building_from_1735_by_D_Ramey_Logan.jpg/440px-Annapolis_Old_Treasury_Building_from_1735_by_D_Ramey_Logan.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Annapolis_Old_Treasury_Building_from_1735_by_D_Ramey_Logan.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         The"Old Treasury Building" on State Circle (adjacent to the\n         <a href="/wiki/Maryland_State_House" title="Maryland State House">\n          Maryland State House\n         </a>\n         ) was built in 1735 and is the oldest standing government building in Annapolis\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:View_of_Annapolis_in_1797_(NYPL_b12612010-423603).tiff">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2728" data-file-width="3536" height="170" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/View_of_Annapolis_in_1797_%28NYPL_b12612010-423603%29.tiff/lossy-page1-220px-View_of_Annapolis_in_1797_%28NYPL_b12612010-423603%29.tiff.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/View_of_Annapolis_in_1797_%28NYPL_b12612010-423603%29.tiff/lossy-page1-330px-View_of_Annapolis_in_1797_%28NYPL_b12612010-423603%29.tiff.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/View_of_Annapolis_in_1797_%28NYPL_b12612010-423603%29.tiff/lossy-page1-440px-View_of_Annapolis_in_1797_%28NYPL_b12612010-423603%29.tiff.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:View_of_Annapolis_in_1797_(NYPL_b12612010-423603).tiff" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <i>\n          View of Annapolis in 1797\n         </i>\n         ,\n         <a class="external text" href="https://commons.wikimedia.org/wiki/File:View_of_Annapolis_in_1797_(NYPL_b12612010-423603).tiff">\n          New York Public Library\n         </a>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       A settlement in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Province_of_Maryland" title="Province of Maryland">\n        Province of Maryland\n       </a>\n       named "Providence" was founded on the north shore of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Severn_River_(Maryland)" title="Severn River (Maryland)">\n        Severn River\n       </a>\n       on the middle\n       <a href="/wiki/Western_Shore_of_Maryland" title="Western Shore of Maryland">\n        Western Shore\n       </a>\n       of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Chesapeake_Bay" title="Chesapeake Bay">\n        Chesapeake Bay\n       </a>\n       in 1649 by\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Puritan" title="Puritan">\n        Puritan\n       </a>\n       exiles from\n       <a href="/wiki/Colony_of_Virginia" title="Colony of Virginia">\n        the Province/Dominion of Virginia\n       </a>\n       led by third Proprietary Governor\n       <a href="/wiki/William_Stone_(Maryland_governor)" title="William Stone (Maryland governor)">\n        William Stone\n       </a>\n       (1603\xe2\x80\x931660). The settlers later moved to a better-protected harbor on the south shore. The settlement on the south shore was initially named "Town at Proctor\'s," then "Town at the Severn," and later "\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anne_Arundel" title="Anne Arundel">\n        Anne Arundel\n       </a>\n       \'s Towne" (after Lady\n       <a href="/wiki/Anne_Arundell" title="Anne Arundell">\n        Ann Arundell\n       </a>\n       (1616-1649), the wife of\n       <a href="/wiki/Cecil_Calvert,_2nd_Baron_Baltimore" title="Cecil Calvert, 2nd Baron Baltimore">\n        Cecilus Calvert, second Lord Baltimore\n       </a>\n       , who died soon afterwards).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Annals_6-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Annals-6">\n         [6]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In 1654, after the\n       <a href="/wiki/Third_English_Civil_War" title="Third English Civil War">\n        Third English Civil War\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Parliamentary" title="Parliamentary">\n        Parliamentary\n       </a>\n       forces assumed control of the Maryland colony and Stone went into exile further south across the\n       <a href="/wiki/Potomac_River" title="Potomac River">\n        Potomac River\n       </a>\n       in\n       <a href="/wiki/Virginia" title="Virginia">\n        Virginia\n       </a>\n       . Per orders from\n       <a href="/wiki/Charles_Calvert,_5th_Baron_Baltimore" title="Charles Calvert, 5th Baron Baltimore">\n        Charles Calvert, fifth Lord Baltimore\n       </a>\n       , Stone returned the following spring at the head of a\n       <a href="/wiki/Cavalier" title="Cavalier">\n        Cavalier\n       </a>\n       royalist force, loyal to the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/King_of_England" title="King of England">\n        King of England\n       </a>\n       . On March 25, 1655, in what is known as the\n       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Severn" title="Battle of the Severn">\n        Battle of the Severn\n       </a>\n       (first colonial naval battle in\n       <a href="/wiki/North_America" title="North America">\n        North America\n       </a>\n       ), Stone was defeated, taken prisoner, and replaced by\n       <a href="/wiki/Josias_Fendall" title="Josias Fendall">\n        Lt. Gen. Josias Fendall\n       </a>\n       (1628\xe2\x80\x931687) as fifth Proprietary\n       <a href="/wiki/Governor_of_Maryland" title="Governor of Maryland">\n        Governor\n       </a>\n       . Fendall governed Maryland during the latter half of the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/English_Commonwealth" title="English Commonwealth">\n        Commonwealth\n       </a>\n       period in\n       <a href="/wiki/England" title="England">\n        England\n       </a>\n       . In 1660, he was replaced by\n       <a href="/wiki/Phillip_Calvert_(governor)" title="Phillip Calvert (governor)">\n        Phillip Calvert\n       </a>\n       (1626\xe2\x80\x931682) as fifth/sixth\n       <a href="/wiki/Governor_of_Maryland" title="Governor of Maryland">\n        Governor of Maryland\n       </a>\n       , after the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Restoration_(Colonies)" title="Restoration (Colonies)">\n        restoration\n       </a>\n       of\n       <a href="/wiki/Charles_II_of_England" title="Charles II of England">\n        Charles II\n       </a>\n       (1630\xe2\x80\x931685) as\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/King_of_England" title="King of England">\n        King\n       </a>\n       in\n       <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_England" title="Kingdom of England">\n        England\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In 1694, soon after the overthrow of the Catholic government of second Royal Governor\n       <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Lawrence_(Governor_of_Maryland)" title="Thomas Lawrence (Governor of Maryland)">\n        Thomas Lawrence\n       </a>\n       (1645-1714), then third Royal Governor\n       <a href="/wiki/Francis_Nicholson" title="Francis Nicholson">\n        Francis Nicholson\n       </a>\n       (1655-1727/28, served 1694-1698), moved the capital of the royal colony, the\n       <a href="/wiki/Province_of_Maryland" title="Province of Maryland">\n        Province of Maryland\n       </a>\n       to Anne Arundel\'s Towne and renamed the town Annapolis after\n       <a href="/wiki/Anne,_Queen_of_Great_Britain" title="Anne, Queen of Great Britain">\n        Princess Anne of Denmark and Norway\n       </a>\n       , soon to be the\n       <a href="/wiki/Queen_regnant" title="Queen regnant">\n        Queen Anne\n       </a>\n       of\n       <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Great_Britain" title="Kingdom of Great Britain">\n        Great Britain\n       </a>\n       (1665-1714, reigned 1702-1714). Annapolis was incorporated as a city in 1708.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7">\n        <a href="#cite_note-7">\n         [7]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       17th century Annapolis was little more than a village, but it grew rapidly for most of the 18th century until the\n       <a href="/wiki/American_Revolutionary_War" title="American Revolutionary War">\n        American Revolutionary War\n       </a>\n       as a political and administrative capital, a\n       <a href="/wiki/Port_of_entry" title="Port of entry">\n        port of entry\n       </a>\n       , and a major center of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_slave_trade" title="Atlantic slave trade">\n        Atlantic slave trade\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8">\n        <a href="#cite_note-8">\n         [8]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Maryland_Gazette" title="Maryland Gazette">\n         Maryland Gazette\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       , which became an important weekly journal, was founded there by Jonas Green\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9">\n        <a href="#cite_note-9">\n         [9]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10">\n        <a href="#cite_note-10">\n         [10]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       in 1745; in 1769 a theatre was opened; during this period also the commerce was considerable, but declined rapidly after Baltimore, with its deeper harbor, was made a port of entry in 1780.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EB1911_11-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-EB1911-11">\n         [11]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Water trades such as oyster-packing, boatbuilding and sailmaking became the city\'s chief industries. Annapolis is home to a large number of recreational boats that have largely replaced the seafood industry in the city.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Hamilton_(Maryland_doctor)" title="Alexander Hamilton (Maryland doctor)">\n        Dr. Alexander Hamilton\n       </a>\n       (1712\xe2\x80\x931756) was a Scottish-born doctor and writer who lived and worked in Annapolis. Leo Lemay says his 1744 travel diary\n       <i>\n        Gentleman\'s Progress: The Itinerarium of Dr. Alexander Hamilton\n       </i>\n       is "the best single portrait of men and manners, of rural and urban life, of the wide range of society and scenery in colonial America."\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12">\n        <a href="#cite_note-12">\n         [12]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:John_Shaw_Flag_(Red_First).svg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1170" data-file-width="2760" height="85" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/John_Shaw_Flag_%28Red_First%29.svg/200px-John_Shaw_Flag_%28Red_First%29.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/John_Shaw_Flag_%28Red_First%29.svg/300px-John_Shaw_Flag_%28Red_First%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/John_Shaw_Flag_%28Red_First%29.svg/400px-John_Shaw_Flag_%28Red_First%29.svg.png 2x" width="200"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:John_Shaw_Flag_(Red_First).svg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         John Shaw Flag (red first variation)\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:John_Shaw_Flag_(White_First).svg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1170" data-file-width="2760" height="85" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/John_Shaw_Flag_%28White_First%29.svg/200px-John_Shaw_Flag_%28White_First%29.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/John_Shaw_Flag_%28White_First%29.svg/300px-John_Shaw_Flag_%28White_First%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/John_Shaw_Flag_%28White_First%29.svg/400px-John_Shaw_Flag_%28White_First%29.svg.png 2x" width="200"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:John_Shaw_Flag_(White_First).svg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         John Shaw Flag (white first variation)\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Annapolis became the temporary capital of the United States after the signing of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Paris_(1783)" title="Treaty of Paris (1783)">\n        Treaty of Paris\n       </a>\n       in 1783. Congress was in session in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Maryland_State_House" title="Maryland State House">\n        state house\n       </a>\n       from November 26, 1783 to June 3, 1784, and it was in Annapolis on December 23, 1783, that\n       <a href="/wiki/George_Washington_in_the_American_Revolution" title="George Washington in the American Revolution">\n        General\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/George_Washington" title="George Washington">\n        Washington\n       </a>\n       resigned his commission as commander-in-chief of the Continental Army.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EB1911_11-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-EB1911-11">\n         [11]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       For the 1783 Congress, the Governor of Maryland commissioned John Shaw, a local cabinet maker, to create an American flag. The flag is slightly different from other designs of the time. The blue field extends over the entire height of the hoist. Shaw created two versions of the flag: one which started with a red stripe and another that started with a white one.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13">\n        <a href="#cite_note-13">\n         [13]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14">\n        <a href="#cite_note-14">\n         [14]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In 1786, delegates from all states of the Union were invited to meet in Annapolis to consider measures for the better regulation of commerce. Delegates from only five states\xe2\x80\x94\n       <a href="/wiki/New_York_(state)" title="New York (state)">\n        New York\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania" title="Pennsylvania">\n        Pennsylvania\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Virginia" title="Virginia">\n        Virginia\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/New_Jersey" title="New Jersey">\n        New Jersey\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Delaware" title="Delaware">\n        Delaware\n       </a>\n       \xe2\x80\x94actually attended the convention, known afterward as the "\n       <a href="/wiki/Annapolis_Convention_(1786)" title="Annapolis Convention (1786)">\n        Annapolis Convention\n       </a>\n       ." Without proceeding to the business for which they had met, the delegates passed a resolution calling for another convention to meet at\n       <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia" title="Philadelphia">\n        Philadelphia\n       </a>\n       in the following year to amend the Articles of Confederation. The Philadelphia convention drafted and approved the Constitution of the United States, which is still in force.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EB1911_11-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-EB1911-11">\n         [11]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span id="Civil_War_era_(1849_\xe2\x80\x93_late_1800s)">\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Civil_War_era_.281849_.E2.80.93_late_1800s.29">\n        Civil War era (1849 \xe2\x80\x93 late 1800s)\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Annapolis,_Maryland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Civil War era (1849 \xe2\x80\x93 late 1800s)">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       During this period, a prisoner of war\n       <a href="/wiki/Parole_camp" title="Parole camp">\n        parole camp\n       </a>\n       , Camp Parole, was set up in Annapolis. As the war continued, the camp expanded to a larger location just west of the city. The area is still referred to as\n       <a href="/wiki/Parole,_Maryland" title="Parole, Maryland">\n        Parole\n       </a>\n       . Wounded Union soldiers and Confederate prisoners were brought by sea to a major hospital in Annapolis.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15">\n        <a href="#cite_note-15">\n         [15]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span id="Contemporary_(1900s\xe2\x80\x93present)">\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Contemporary_.281900s.E2.80.93present.29">\n        Contemporary (1900s\xe2\x80\x93present)\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Annapolis,_Maryland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Contemporary (1900s\xe2\x80\x93present)">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:402px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Annapolis_panoramic_view_from_State_House,_1911.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="620" data-file-width="2565" height="97" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Annapolis_panoramic_view_from_State_House%2C_1911.jpg/400px-Annapolis_panoramic_view_from_State_House%2C_1911.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Annapolis_panoramic_view_from_State_House%2C_1911.jpg/600px-Annapolis_panoramic_view_from_State_House%2C_1911.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Annapolis_panoramic_view_from_State_House%2C_1911.jpg/800px-Annapolis_panoramic_view_from_State_House%2C_1911.jpg 2x" width="400"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Annapolis_panoramic_view_from_State_House,_1911.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         View of Annapolis from the State House dome, 1911\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       In 1900, Annapolis had a population of 8,585.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16">\n        <a href="#cite_note-16">\n         [16]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       To the north of the state house is a monument to\n       <a href="/wiki/Thurgood_Marshall" title="Thurgood Marshall">\n        Thurgood Marshall\n       </a>\n       , the first black justice of the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/US_Supreme_Court" title="US Supreme Court">\n        US Supreme Court\n       </a>\n       and formerly a Maryland lawyer who won many important\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Civil_rights" title="Civil rights">\n        civil rights\n       </a>\n       cases.\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:USPS_Annapolis_Main_post_office.JPG">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2112" data-file-width="2816" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/USPS_Annapolis_Main_post_office.JPG/220px-USPS_Annapolis_Main_post_office.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/USPS_Annapolis_Main_post_office.JPG/330px-USPS_Annapolis_Main_post_office.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/USPS_Annapolis_Main_post_office.JPG/440px-USPS_Annapolis_Main_post_office.JPG 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:USPS_Annapolis_Main_post_office.JPG" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Former USPS Annapolis Main post office\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Close by are the state treasury building, erected late in the 17th century for the House of Delegates; Saint Anne\'s Protestant Episcopal church, in later colonial days a state church; a statue of\n       <a href="/wiki/Roger_B._Taney" title="Roger B. Taney">\n        Roger B. Taney\n       </a>\n       (by W.H. Rinehart); and a statue of Baron\n       <a href="/wiki/Johann_de_Kalb" title="Johann de Kalb">\n        Johann de Kalb\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EB1911_11-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-EB1911-11">\n         [11]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       On December 21, 1906, Henry Davis was lynched in the city. He was suspected of assaulting a local woman. Nobody was ever tried for the crime.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17">\n        <a href="#cite_note-17">\n         [17]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Annapolis has many 18th-century houses. The names of several of the streets\xe2\x80\x94King George\'s, Prince George\'s, Hanover, and Duke of Gloucester, etc.\xe2\x80\x94date from colonial days.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EB1911_11-4">\n        <a href="#cite_note-EB1911-11">\n         [11]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The United States Naval Academy was founded here in 1845. During World War II, shipyards in Annapolis built a number of PT Boats, and military vessels such as minesweepers and patrol boats were built in Annapolis during the Korean and Vietnam wars.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18">\n        <a href="#cite_note-18">\n         [18]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       It was at Annapolis in July 1940 that\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Grand_Duchess_Charlotte_of_Luxembourg" title="Grand Duchess Charlotte of Luxembourg">\n        Grand Duchess Charlotte of Luxembourg\n       </a>\n       arrived in exile during World War II.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19">\n        <a href="#cite_note-19">\n         [19]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In the summer of 1984, the Navy Marine Corps Memorial Stadium in Annapolis hosted soccer games as part of the\n       <a href="/wiki/1984_Summer_Olympics" title="1984 Summer Olympics">\n        XXIII Olympiad\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       During September 18\xe2\x80\x9319, 2003,\n       <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Isabel" title="Hurricane Isabel">\n        Hurricane Isabel\n       </a>\n       created the largest storm surge known in Annapolis\'s history, cresting at\n       <span style="white-space:nowrap">\n        7.58\xc2\xa0ft (2.31\xc2\xa0m)\n       </span>\n       . Much of downtown Annapolis was flooded and many businesses and homes in outlying areas were damaged.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20">\n        <a href="#cite_note-20">\n         [20]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The previous record was 6.35 feet (1.94\xc2\xa0m) during a hurricane in 1933, and\n       <span style="white-space:nowrap">\n        5.5\xc2\xa0ft (1.7\xc2\xa0m)\n       </span>\n       during\n       <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Hazel" title="Hurricane Hazel">\n        Hurricane Hazel\n       </a>\n       in 1954.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The 1998 Comprehensive Plan will soon\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers">\n          <span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (February 2016)">\n           when?\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n       be replaced with a new document, containing initiatives and directives of the city government on development and infrastructure. This process was mandated by Maryland state law in the Economic Growth, Resource Protection, and Planning Act of 1992.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21">\n        <a href="#cite_note-21">\n         [21]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Annapolis_Charter_300&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Annapolis Charter 300 (page does not exist)">\n        Annapolis Charter 300\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/EnVISIONing_Annapolis" title="EnVISIONing Annapolis">\n        EnVISIONing Annapolis\n       </a>\n       co-sponsored a public lecture series from September 2007 through June 2008 exploring these issues.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       From mid-2007 through December 2008, the city celebrated the 300th anniversary of its 1708 Royal Charter, which established democratic self-governance. The many cultural events of this celebration were organized by Annapolis Charter 300.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Railway">\n        Railway\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Annapolis,_Maryland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Railway">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Annapolis is the only capital city in America east of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Mississippi_River" title="Mississippi River">\n        Mississippi River\n       </a>\n       without rail transport of any sort. From 1840 to 1968, Annapolis was connected to the outside world by railroad. The\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Washington,_Baltimore_and_Annapolis_Railroad" title="Washington, Baltimore and Annapolis Railroad">\n        Washington, Baltimore and Annapolis Railroad\n       </a>\n       (WB&amp;A) operated two electrified\n       <a href="/wiki/Interurban" title="Interurban">\n        interurban\n       </a>\n       lines that brought passengers into the city from both the South and the North. The southern route ran down King George Street and Main Street, leading directly to the statehouse, while the northern route entered town via\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Glen_Burnie" title="Glen Burnie">\n        Glen Burnie\n       </a>\n       . In 1935, the WB&amp;A went bankrupt due to the effects of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Great_Depression" title="Great Depression">\n        Great Depression\n       </a>\n       and suspended service along its southern route, while the newly created\n       <a href="/wiki/Baltimore_and_Annapolis_Railroad" title="Baltimore and Annapolis Railroad">\n        Baltimore and Annapolis Railroad\n       </a>\n       (B&amp;A) retained service on the northern route. Steam trains of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Baltimore_and_Ohio_Railroad" title="Baltimore and Ohio Railroad">\n        Baltimore and Ohio Railroad\n       </a>\n       also occasionally operated over the line to Annapolis, primarily for special Naval Academy movements. Passenger rail service on the B&amp;A was eventually discontinued in 1950; freight service ceased in 1968 after the dilapidated trestle crossing the\n       <a href="/wiki/Severn_River_(Maryland)" title="Severn River (Maryland)">\n        Severn River\n       </a>\n       was condemned. The tracks were eventually dismantled in 1976.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22">\n        <a href="#cite_note-22">\n         [22]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_institutions">\n        Notable institutions\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Annapolis,_Maryland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Notable institutions">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Maryland_State_House_from_Church_Circle.JPG">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2757" data-file-width="2273" height="267" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Maryland_State_House_from_Church_Circle.JPG/220px-Maryland_State_House_from_Church_Circle.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Maryland_State_House_from_Church_Circle.JPG/330px-Maryland_State_House_from_Church_Circle.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Maryland_State_House_from_Church_Circle.JPG/440px-Maryland_State_House_from_Church_Circle.JPG 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Maryland_State_House_from_Church_Circle.JPG" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Maryland State House as seen from Church Circle\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="The_State_House">\n        The State House\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Annapolis,_Maryland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: The State House">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/Maryland_State_House" title="Maryland State House">\n        Maryland State House\n       </a>\n       is the oldest in continuous legislative use in the United States. Construction started in 1772, and the Maryland legislature first met there in 1779. It is topped by the largest wooden dome built without nails in the country. The Maryland State House housed the workings of the United States government from November 26, 1783, to August 13, 1784, and the\n       <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Paris_(1783)" title="Treaty of Paris (1783)">\n        Treaty of Paris\n       </a>\n       was ratified there on January 14, 1784, so Annapolis became the first peacetime capital of the U.S.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23">\n        <a href="#cite_note-23">\n         [23]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-State_House_24-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-State_House-24">\n         [24]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       It was in the Maryland State House that\n       <a href="/wiki/George_Washington" title="George Washington">\n        George Washington\n       </a>\n       famously resigned his commission before the\n       <a href="/wiki/Continental_Congress" title="Continental Congress">\n        Continental Congress\n       </a>\n       on December 23, 1783.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-State_House_24-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-State_House-24">\n         [24]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="United_States_Naval_Academy">\n        United States Naval Academy\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Annapolis,_Maryland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: United States Naval Academy">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bfc_annapolis_md_usna_bancroft_hall_01w.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="197" data-file-width="390" height="111" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Bfc_annapolis_md_usna_bancroft_hall_01w.jpg/220px-Bfc_annapolis_md_usna_bancroft_hall_01w.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Bfc_annapolis_md_usna_bancroft_hall_01w.jpg/330px-Bfc_annapolis_md_usna_bancroft_hall_01w.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/8/86/Bfc_annapolis_md_usna_bancroft_hall_01w.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bfc_annapolis_md_usna_bancroft_hall_01w.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         US Naval Academy,\n         <a href="/wiki/Bancroft_Hall" title="Bancroft Hall">\n          Bancroft Hall\n         </a>\n         (c. 1908)\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Naval_Academy" title="United States Naval Academy">\n        United States Naval Academy\n       </a>\n       was founded in 1845 on the site of\n       <a href="/wiki/Fort_Severn" title="Fort Severn">\n        Fort Severn\n       </a>\n       , and now occupies an area of land\n       <a href="/wiki/Land_reclamation" title="Land reclamation">\n        reclaimed\n       </a>\n       from the\n       <a href="/wiki/Severn_River_(Maryland)" title="Severn River (Maryland)">\n        Severn River\n       </a>\n       next to the\n       <a href="/wiki/Chesapeake_Bay" title="Chesapeake Bay">\n        Chesapeake Bay\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span id="St._John\'s_College">\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="St._John.27s_College">\n        St. John\'s College\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Annapolis,_Maryland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: St. John\'s College">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Annapolis is the seat of\n       <a href="/wiki/St._John%27s_College_(Annapolis/Santa_Fe)" title="St. John\'s College (Annapolis/Santa Fe)">\n        St. John\'s College\n       </a>\n       , a non-sectarian private college that was once supported by the state; it was opened in 1789 as the successor of King William\'s School, which was founded by an act of the Maryland legislature in 1696 and was opened in 1701. Its principal building, McDowell Hall, was originally to be the governor\'s mansion; although \xc2\xa34,000 was appropriated to build it in 1742, it was not completed until after the War of Independence.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EB1911_11-5">\n        <a href="#cite_note-EB1911-11">\n         [11]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25">\n        <a href="#cite_note-25">\n         [25]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Theater">\n        Theater\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Annapolis,_Maryland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Theater">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Annapolis has a thriving community theater scene which includes two venues in the historic district.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       On East Street,\n       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Colonial_Players&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Colonial Players (page does not exist)">\n        Colonial Players\n       </a>\n       produces approximately six shows a year in its 180-seat theater.\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/A_Christmas_Carol" title="A Christmas Carol">\n         A Christmas Carol\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       has been a seasonal tradition in Annapolis since it opened at the Colonial Players theater in 1981. Based on the play by\n       <a href="/wiki/Charles_Dickens" title="Charles Dickens">\n        Charles Dickens\n       </a>\n       , the 90-minute production by the Colonial Players is an original musical adaptation, with play and lyrics by Richard Wade and music by Dick Gessner. Colonial Players, Inc. is a nonprofit organization founded in 1949. Its first production,\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/The_Male_Animal" title="The Male Animal">\n         The Male Animal\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       , was performed in 1949 at the Annapolis Recreation Center on Compromise Street. In 1955, the organization moved to its venue in a former automotive repair shop on East Street.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26">\n        <a href="#cite_note-26">\n         [26]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27">\n        <a href="#cite_note-27">\n         [27]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       During the warmer months,\n       <a href="/wiki/Annapolis_Summer_Garden_Theatre" title="Annapolis Summer Garden Theatre">\n        Annapolis Summer Garden Theatre\n       </a>\n       presents three shows on its outdoor stage, which is visible from the City Dock. A nonprofit organization, Annapolis Summer Garden Theatre has been providing "theatre under the stars" since 1966, when it performed\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/You_Can%27t_Take_It_with_You_(play)" title="You Can\'t Take It with You (play)">\n         You Can\'t Take It with You\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       and\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Brigadoon" title="Brigadoon">\n         Brigadoon\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       at Carvel Hall Hotel. It began leasing its site at 143 Compromise Street, the former location of the Shaw Blacksmith Shop, in 1967, and became owner of the property in 1990.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28">\n        <a href="#cite_note-28">\n         [28]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29">\n        <a href="#cite_note-29">\n         [29]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30">\n        <a href="#cite_note-30">\n         [30]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The Naval Academy Masqueraders, a theater group at the United State Naval Academy, produces one "main-stage show" each fall and student-directed one-act plays in the spring. Founded in 1847, the Masqueraders is the oldest extracurricular activity at the Naval Academy. Its shows, performed in Mahan Hall, are selected to support the Academy\'s English curriculum.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31">\n        <a href="#cite_note-31">\n         [31]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The King William Players, a student theater group at\n       <a href="/wiki/St._John%27s_College_(Annapolis/Santa_Fe)" title="St. John\'s College (Annapolis/Santa Fe)">\n        St. John\'s College\n       </a>\n       , holds two performances each semester in the college\'s Francis Scott Key Auditorium. Admission is usually free and open to the public.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32">\n        <a href="#cite_note-32">\n         [32]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span id="Museums,_historical_sites,_and_monuments">\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Museums.2C_historical_sites.2C_and_monuments">\n        Museums, historical sites, and monuments\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Annapolis,_Maryland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Museums, historical sites, and monuments">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:262px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Annapolis_Harbor_alongside_Dock_Street_by_D_Ramey_Logan.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1043" data-file-width="1871" height="145" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Annapolis_Harbor_alongside_Dock_Street_by_D_Ramey_Logan.jpg/260px-Annapolis_Harbor_alongside_Dock_Street_by_D_Ramey_Logan.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Annapolis_Harbor_alongside_Dock_Street_by_D_Ramey_Logan.jpg/390px-Annapolis_Harbor_alongside_Dock_Street_by_D_Ramey_Logan.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Annapolis_Harbor_alongside_Dock_Street_by_D_Ramey_Logan.jpg/520px-Annapolis_Harbor_alongside_Dock_Street_by_D_Ramey_Logan.jpg 2x" width="260"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Annapolis_Harbor_alongside_Dock_Street_by_D_Ramey_Logan.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Over Annapolis Harbor &amp; Dock Street\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:262px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Maryland_World_War_II_Memorial.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1664" data-file-width="2496" height="173" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Maryland_World_War_II_Memorial.jpg/260px-Maryland_World_War_II_Memorial.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Maryland_World_War_II_Memorial.jpg/390px-Maryland_World_War_II_Memorial.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Maryland_World_War_II_Memorial.jpg/520px-Maryland_World_War_II_Memorial.jpg 2x" width="260"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Maryland_World_War_II_Memorial.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Maryland World War II Memorial\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/Banneker-Douglass_Museum" title="Banneker-Douglass Museum">\n        Banneker-Douglass Museum\n       </a>\n       , located in the historic Mount Moriah Church at 87 Franklin Street, documents the history of African Americans in Maryland. Since its opening on February 24, 1984, the museum has provided educational programs, rotating exhibits, and a research facility. Admission is free.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33">\n        <a href="#cite_note-33">\n         [33]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/U.S._Naval_Academy_Museum" title="U.S. Naval Academy Museum">\n        Preble Hall\n       </a>\n       , named for\n       <a href="/wiki/Edward_Preble" title="Edward Preble">\n        Edward Preble\n       </a>\n       , houses the U.S. Naval Academy Museum, founded in 1845. Its Beverley R. Robinson Collection contains 6,000 prints depicting European and American naval history from 1514 through World War II. It is also home to one of the world\'s best ship model collections, donated by\n       <a href="/wiki/Henry_Huttleston_Rogers" title="Henry Huttleston Rogers">\n        Henry Huttleston Rogers\n       </a>\n       . Rogers\'s donation was the impetus for the construction of Preble Hall. The museum has approximately 100,000 visitors each year.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34">\n        <a href="#cite_note-34">\n         [34]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hammond-Harwood_House" title="Hammond-Harwood House">\n        Hammond-Harwood House\n       </a>\n       , located at 19 Maryland Avenue, was built in 1774 for Matthias Hammond, a wealthy Maryland farmer. Its design was adapted by\n       <a href="/wiki/William_Buckland_(architect)" title="William Buckland (architect)">\n        William Buckland (architect)\n       </a>\n       from\n       <a href="/wiki/Andrea_Palladio" title="Andrea Palladio">\n        Andrea Palladio\n       </a>\n       \'s\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Villa_Pisani" title="Villa Pisani">\n        Villa Pisani\n       </a>\n       to accommodate American Colonial regional preferences. Since 1940, when the house was purchased from St. John\'s College by the Hammond-Harwood House Association, it has served as a museum exhibiting a collection of John Shaw furniture and\n       <a href="/wiki/Charles_Willson_Peale" title="Charles Willson Peale">\n        Charles Willson Peale\n       </a>\n       paintings. Its exterior and interior preserve the original architecture of a mansion from the late Colonial period.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35">\n        <a href="#cite_note-35">\n         [35]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36">\n        <a href="#cite_note-36">\n         [36]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/Kunta_Kinte" title="Kunta Kinte">\n        Kunta Kinte\n       </a>\n       -\n       <a href="/wiki/Alex_Haley" title="Alex Haley">\n        Alex Haley\n       </a>\n       memorial, located at the head of the city\'s harbor, commemorates the arrival point of Alex Haley\'s African ancestor, Kunta Kinte, whose story is related in Haley\'s book\n       <i>\n        Roots\n       </i>\n       . A sculpture group at the memorial site portrays Alex Haley seated, reading from a book to three children. The final phase of the memorial\'s construction was completed in 2002.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37">\n        <a href="#cite_note-37">\n         [37]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/Paca_House_and_Garden" title="Paca House and Garden">\n        Paca House and Garden\n       </a>\n       encompasses an 18th-century Georgian mansion constructed by\n       <a href="/wiki/William_Paca" title="William Paca">\n        William Paca\n       </a>\n       , a signer of the Declaration of Independence. The property includes a terraced garden that has been restored to its colonial-era design.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38">\n        <a href="#cite_note-38">\n         [38]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Other">\n        Other\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Annapolis,_Maryland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Other">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       The Annapolis area was the home of a\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/VLF" title="VLF">\n        VLF\n       </a>\n       -transmitter called\n       <a href="/wiki/NSS_Annapolis" title="NSS Annapolis">\n        NSS Annapolis\n       </a>\n       , which was used by the United States Navy to communicate with its Atlantic submarine fleet. Annapolis often serves as the end point for the 3,000-mile annual transcontinental\n       <a href="/wiki/Race_Across_America" title="Race Across America">\n        Race Across America\n       </a>\n       bicycle race.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="2007_Annapolis_Conference">\n        2007 Annapolis Conference\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Annapolis,_Maryland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: 2007 Annapolis Conference">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Annapolis_Conference" title="Annapolis Conference">\n        Annapolis Conference\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       As announced by\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Secretary_of_State" title="United States Secretary of State">\n        United States Secretary of State\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/Condoleezza_Rice" title="Condoleezza Rice">\n        Condoleezza Rice\n       </a>\n       , Annapolis was the venue for a Middle East summit dealing with the\n       <a href="/wiki/Israeli%E2%80%93Palestinian_peace_process" title="Israeli\xe2\x80\x93Palestinian peace process">\n        Israeli\xe2\x80\x93Palestinian peace process\n       </a>\n       , with the participation of Israeli Prime Minister\n       <a href="/wiki/Ehud_Olmert" title="Ehud Olmert">\n        Ehud Olmert\n       </a>\n       , Palestinian President\n       <a href="/wiki/Mahmoud_Abbas" title="Mahmoud Abbas">\n        Mahmoud Abbas\n       </a>\n       ("\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Abu_Mazen" title="Abu Mazen">\n        Abu Mazen\n       </a>\n       ") and various other leaders from the region. The conference was held on Monday, November 26, 2007.\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Geography_and_climate">\n        Geography and climate\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Annapolis,_Maryland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Geography and climate">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="thumb tleft">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Annapolis_Maryland.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2008" data-file-width="3032" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Annapolis_Maryland.jpg/220px-Annapolis_Maryland.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Annapolis_Maryland.jpg/330px-Annapolis_Maryland.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Annapolis_Maryland.jpg/440px-Annapolis_Maryland.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Annapolis_Maryland.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Early-March 2002 astronaut photography of Annapolis Maryland taken from the International Space Station (ISS)\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Located 25 miles (40\xc2\xa0km) south of Baltimore and 30 miles (48\xc2\xa0km) east of Washington D.C., Annapolis is the closest state capital to the national capital.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39">\n        <a href="#cite_note-39">\n         [39]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The city is a part of the Atlantic Coastal Plain, and is relatively flat, with the highest point being only 50 feet (15\xc2\xa0m) above sea level.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       According to the\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Census_Bureau" title="United States Census Bureau">\n        United States Census Bureau\n       </a>\n       , the city has a total area of 8.10 square miles (20.98\xc2\xa0km\n       <sup>\n        2\n       </sup>\n       ), of which 7.18 square miles (18.60\xc2\xa0km\n       <sup>\n        2\n       </sup>\n       ) is land and 0.92 square miles (2.38\xc2\xa0km\n       <sup>\n        2\n       </sup>\n       ) is water.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-QuickFacts_2-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-QuickFacts-2">\n         [2]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USA_3-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-USA-3">\n         [3]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Annapolis lies within the\n       <a href="/wiki/Humid_subtropical_climate" title="Humid subtropical climate">\n        humid subtropical climate\n       </a>\n       zone (\n       <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="K\xc3\xb6ppen climate classification">\n        K\xc3\xb6ppen\n       </a>\n       <i>\n        Cfa\n       </i>\n       ), with hot, humid summers, cool winters, and generous precipitation year-round. Low elevation and proximity to the Chesapeake Bay give the area more moderate spring and summertime temperatures and slightly less extreme winter lows than locations further inland, such as Washington, D.C.\n      </p>\n      <table class="wikitable collapsible" style="width:90%; text-align:center; font-size:90%; line-height: 1.2em; margin:auto;">\n       <tr>\n        <th ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="thumb tleft">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">\n        <a class="image" </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td colspan="4" style="border-top:1px solid black; font-size:85%; text-align:left">\n         <a class="external text" href="http://www.census.gov/prod/www/abs/decennial/" rel="nofollow">\n          U.S. Decennial Census\n         </a>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="2010_census">\n        2010 census\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Annapolis,_Maryland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: 2010 census">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       As of the census\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FactFinder_43-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-FactFinder-43">\n         [43]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       of 2010, there were 38,394 people, 16,136 households, and 8,776 families residing in the city. The population density was 5,347.4 inhabitants per square mile (2,064.6/km\n       <sup>\n        2\n       </sup>\n       ). There were 17,845 housing units at an average density of 2,485.4 per square mile (959.6/km\n       <sup>\n        2\n       </sup>\n       ). The racial makeup of the city was 60.1%\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/White_(U.S._Census)" title="White (U.S. Census)">\n        White\n       </a>\n       , 26.0%\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/African_American_(U.S._Census)" title="African American (U.S. Census)">\n        African American\n       </a>\n       , 0.3%\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Native_American_(U.S._Census)" title="Native American (U.S. Census)">\n        Native American\n       </a>\n       , 2.1%\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Asian_(U.S._Census)" title="Asian (U.S. Census)">\n        Asian\n       </a>\n       , 9.0% from\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Race_(U.S._Census)" title="Race (U.S. Census)">\n        other races\n       </a>\n       , and 2.6% from two or more races.\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hispanic_(U.S._Census)" title="Hispanic (U.S. Census)">\n        Hispanic\n       </a>\n       or\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Latino_(U.S._Census)" title="Latino (U.S. Census)">\n        Latino\n       </a>\n       of any race were 16.8% of the population.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       There were 16,136 households, of which 26.6% had children under the age of 18 living with them, 35.3% were married couples living together, 14.9% had a female householder with no husband present, 4.2% had a male householder with no wife present, and 45.6% were non-families. 35.0% of all households were made up of individuals and 11.1% had someone living alone who was 65 years of age or older. The average household size was 2.34 and the average family size was 3.02.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The median age in the city was 36 years. 20.8% of residents were under the age of 18; 9.9% were between the ages of 18 and 24; 31.1% were from 25 to 44; 25.3% were from 45 to 64; and 13% were 65 years of age or older. The gender makeup of the city was 47.8% male and 52.2% female.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="2000_census">\n        2000 census\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Annapolis,_Maryland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: 2000 census">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       As of the census\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GR2_44-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-GR2-44">\n         [44]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       of 2000, there were 35,838 people, 15,303 households, and 8,676 families residing in the city. The population density was 5,326.0 people per square mile (2,056.0/km\xc2\xb2). There were 16,165 housing units at an average density of 2,402.3 per square mile (927.4/km\xc2\xb2). The racial makeup of the city was 62.66%\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/White_(U.S._Census)" title="White (U.S. Census)">\n        White\n       </a>\n       , 31.44% Black or\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/African_American_(U.S._Census)" title="African American (U.S. Census)">\n        African American\n       </a>\n       , 0.17%\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Native_American_(U.S._Census)" title="Native American (U.S. Census)">\n        Native American\n       </a>\n       , 1.81%\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Asian_(U.S._Census)" title="Asian (U.S. Census)">\n        Asian\n       </a>\n       , 0.03%\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pacific_Islander_(U.S._Census)" title="Pacific Islander (U.S. Census)">\n        Pacific Islander\n       </a>\n       , 2.22% from other races, and 1.67% from two or more races. 8.42% of the population were\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hispanics_in_the_United_States" title="Hispanics in the United States">\n        Hispanic\n       </a>\n       or\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Latino_(U.S._Census)" title="Latino (U.S. Census)">\n        Latino\n       </a>\n       of any race.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       There were 15,303 households, out of which 24.5% had children under the age of 18 living with them, 36.6% were married couples living together, 16.3% had a female householder with no husband present, and 43.3% were non-families. 32.9% of all households were made up of individuals and 9.2% had someone living alone who was 65 years of age or older. The average household size was 2.30 and the average family size was 2.93.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In the city, the population was spread out with 21.7% under the age of 18, 9.3% from 18 to 24, 33.4% from 25 to 44, 23.7% from 45 to 64, and 11.9% who were 65 years of age or older. The median age was 36 years. For every 100 females there were 90.0 males. For every 100 females age 18 and over there were 86.8 males age 18 and over.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The median income for a household in the city was $49,243, and the median income for a family was $56,984 (these figures had risen to $70,140 and $84,573 respectively, according to a 2007 estimate\n       <sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">\n        <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Annapolis,_Maryland&amp;action=edit">\n         [update]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       ).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45">\n        <a href="#cite_note-45">\n         [45]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Males had a median income of $39,548 versus $30,741 for females. The per capita income for the city was $27,180. About 9.5% of families and 12.7% of the population were living in poverty, of which 20.8% were under age 18 and 10.4% were age 65 or over.\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tnone" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right:auto; overflow:hidden; width:auto; max-width:908px;">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="">\n        <div class="overflowbugx" style="overflow:auto;">\n         <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Annapolis_Maryland_wide_by_D_Ramey_Logan_with_Grant_Jensen.jpg" title="Annapolis, Maryland">\n          <img alt="" data-file-height="485" data-file-width="1493" height="292" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Annapolis_Maryland_wide_by_D_Ramey_Logan_with_Grant_Jensen.jpg/900px-Annapolis_Maryland_wide_by_D_Ramey_Logan_with_Grant_Jensen.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Annapolis_Maryland_wide_by_D_Ramey_Logan_with_Grant_Jensen.jpg/1350px-Annapolis_Maryland_wide_by_D_Ramey_Logan_with_Grant_Jensen.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/e/e3/Annapolis_Maryland_wide_by_D_Ramey_Logan_with_Grant_Jensen.jpg 2x" width="900"/>\n         </a>\n        </div>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a href="/wiki/File:Annapolis_Maryland_wide_by_D_Ramey_Logan_with_Grant_Jensen.jpg" title="File:Annapolis Maryland wide by D Ramey Logan with Grant Jensen.jpg">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Annapolis, Maryland\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">\n        Economy\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Annapolis,_Maryland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18"
